\item A6: Exact equality with the previously chosen minimal P\"oschl--Teller channel potentials is
not automatic.
\[
\boxed{\text{Not proved generally}}
\]
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Projector fluctuation geometry}

Let \(P_B(\xi)\) be a static defect background, and let the full projector be
\[
P(x)=P_B(\xi)+\delta P(y,\xi),
\qquad x=(y,\xi),
\]
where \(y^\mu\) are worldvolume coordinates and \(\xi\) is the transverse coordinate.

Because \(P^2=P\), linearized fluctuations obey
\[
P_B\,\delta P + \delta P\,P_B = \delta P.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\delta P = P_B\,\delta P\,Q_B + Q_B\,\delta P\,P_B,
\qquad
Q_B:=\mathbf 1-P_B.
\]
Thus the fluctuation is tangent to the projector manifold.

Using a local normalized representative
\[
P_B=z_B z_B^\dagger,
\qquad z_B^\dagger z_B=1,
\]
a convenient tangent parametrization is
\[
\delta P = \eta z_B^\dagger + z_B \eta^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger \eta = 0.
\]
Hence
\[
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp.
\]

\paragraph{Proposition 1.}
The physical fluctuation problem reduces to a rank-two complex field \(\eta\) valued in the bundle
\(Q_B\).

\paragraph{Proof.}
This is the standard tangent parametrization of rank-one Hermitian projectors. \(\square\)

\subsection{Quadratic Hessian around a static background}

Expand the action to quadratic order:
\[
S[P_B+\delta P]
=
S[P_B]
+
\delta S[P_B;\delta P]
+
\frac12\delta^2 S[P_B;\delta P]
+\cdots.
\]
Since \(P_B\) solves the background Euler--Lagrange equation,
\[
\delta S[P_B;\delta P]=0.
\]
The quadratic fluctuation action takes the generic form
\[
\delta^2 S
=
\int d^{d+1}x\,
\eta^\dagger
\Bigl[
-\rho\,D_\mu^{(B)}D^{(B)\mu}
+
\mathcal M_B(\xi)
\Bigr]\eta,
\]
where:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(D_\mu^{(B)}\) is the induced connection on \(Q_B\),
\item \(\mathcal M_B(\xi)\) is a Hermitian \(2\times2\) endomorphism built from the defect
background \(P_B(\xi)\) and its derivatives.
\end{enumerate}

Since the background depends only on \(\xi\), we may split
\[
D_\mu^{(B)}D^{(B)\mu}
=
D_y^{(B)\,2}+D_\xi^{(B)\,2}.
\]
Thus the fluctuation operator is of the schematic form
\[
\mathcal H_B
=
-\rho\,D_\xi^{(B)\,2}
-\rho\,D_y^{(B)\,2}
+
\mathcal M_B(\xi).
\]

\paragraph{Theorem 2 (Projector Hessian channel theorem).}
The quadratic fluctuation operator of a static \(CP^2\) projector defect is a matrix
Schr\"odinger operator in the transverse coordinate \(\xi\), with a background-dependent
endomorphism potential on the rank-two bundle \(Q_B\).

\paragraph{Proof.}
Directly from the second variation of the projector sigma-model action. \(\square\)

This already matches the structural form of the minimal effective operator:
\[
-\partial_\xi^2 + U(\xi).
\]

\subsection{Choice of a local \(Q_B\)-frame and channel decomposition}

Choose a local orthonormal frame
\[
e(\xi)=\bigl(e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi)\bigr)
\]
of \(Q_B\). Expanding
\[
\eta(\xi,y)=e_a(\xi)\,\chi^a(\xi,y),
\]
the quadratic operator becomes an operator on the \(\mathbb C^2\)-valued coefficient field
\[
\chi=(\chi^1,\chi^2)^T.
\]
In general,
\[
\mathcal H_B
=
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2
+
\mathcal A_\xi(\xi)\partial_\xi
+
\mathcal U_B(\xi)
-\rho\,\partial_y^2
+\cdots,
\]
where \(\mathcal A_\xi\) arises from the frame connection and \(\mathcal U_B\) is a Hermitian
\(2\times2\) potential matrix.

By a local unitary gauge choice along the one-dimensional transverse line, one may set the
connection to zero locally:
\[
\mathcal A_\xi=0.
\]
Thus, locally,
\[
\mathcal H_B
=
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2
+
\mathcal U_B(\xi)
-\rho\,\partial_y^2
+\cdots.
\]

\paragraph{Corollary 3.}
Locally along the transverse line, the projector Hessian is gauge-equivalent to a matrix
Schr\"odinger operator
\[
-\partial_\xi^2+\mathcal U_B(\xi)
\]
on the internal doublet.

This is the first precise matching with the minimal effective defect operator.

\subsection{Reflection symmetry and parity decomposition}

Assume now that the defect is reflection-symmetric:
\[
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi).
\]
Then, in a reflection-even frame \(e_a(-\xi)=e_a(\xi)\), the coefficient-space potential obeys
\[
\mathcal U_B(-\xi)=\mathcal U_B(\xi).
\]
Hence the static channel operator commutes with reflection
\[
(J\chi)(\xi):=\chi(-\xi).
\]
Therefore the transverse spectrum splits into even and odd channels:
\[
\chi_+(-\xi)=\chi_+(\xi),
\qquad
\chi_-(-\xi)=-\chi_-(\xi).
\]

\paragraph{Theorem 4 (Parity channel decomposition theorem).}
For a reflection-symmetric static defect background, the static projector Hessian decomposes into
even and odd transverse parity sectors.

\paragraph{Proof.}
The operator has even coefficients in \(\xi\), hence commutes with reflection. Standard spectral
decomposition then gives parity eigenchannels. \(\square\)

This is the operator origin of the previously postulated \(f_+\) and \(f_-\) channels.

\subsection{Matching to the minimal scalar channels}

The minimal effective defect model used
\[
H_+=-\partial_\xi^2+U_+(\xi),
\qquad
H_-=-\partial_\xi^2+U_-(\xi),
\]
with
\[
U_+(\xi)=\kappa^2-2\kappa^2\operatorname{sech}^2(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
U_-(\xi)=\kappa^2-6\kappa^2\operatorname{sech}^2(\kappa\xi).
\]
The exact claim that the projector Hessian gives precisely these two P\"oschl--Teller wells is too
strong in general and cannot be proved without the explicit microscopic/effective potential
\(U(P,\partial P,\ldots)\).

However, a weaker and correct matching statement is available:

\paragraph{Theorem 5 (Effective channel matching theorem).}
If the reflection-symmetric projector Hessian has one localized even low mode and one localized odd
low mode in each internal channel, then its low-energy parity-reduced transverse spectrum is
effectively modeled by a pair of scalar channel operators
\[
H_\pm=-\partial_\xi^2+U_\pm^{\mathrm{eff}}(\xi),
\]
for suitable even potentials \(U_\pm^{\mathrm{eff}}(\xi)\). The previously used P\"oschl--Teller
choice is an explicit solvable representative of this effective class.

\paragraph{Proof.}
Given any normalized isolated even/odd low modes \(f_\pm\), one may reconstruct effective scalar
potentials by
\[
U_\pm^{\mathrm{eff}}(\xi)=\frac{f_\pm''(\xi)}{f_\pm(\xi)}.
\]
The P\"oschl--Teller wells are a solvable representative realizing exactly the chosen explicit
profiles. \(\square\)

Thus the relation between the projector Hessian and the minimal model is:
\[
\text{projector Hessian}
\Longrightarrow
\text{parity channels}
\Longrightarrow
\text{effective scalar wells}
\Longrightarrow
\text{explicit P\"oschl--Teller representative}.
\]

\subsection{Origin of the odd transport kernel}

We now turn on slow worldvolume dependence \(y^\mu\). The full Hessian contains mixed terms in
which worldvolume derivatives couple to the \(\xi\)-dependent background structure. Schematically,
the first-order transport piece on the low-energy sector has the form
\[
\mathcal L_1
=
-i\,\mathcal V^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
\]

The key point is that \(\mathcal V^\mu(\xi)\) is built linearly from background tensors that vanish
for a uniform background and measure how the defect varies in \(\xi\). Thus the leading local
candidates are proportional to
\[
\partial_\xi P_B(\xi),
\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B(\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(\xi),
\]
or equivalent frame-covariant combinations.

Since \(P_B(\xi)\) is even, these quantities are odd:
\[
\partial_\xi P_B(-\xi)=-\partial_\xi P_B(\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(-\xi)=-\theta'(\xi).
\]

\paragraph{Theorem 6 (Odd transport kernel matching theorem).}
For a reflection-symmetric projector defect background, any leading worldvolume transport kernel
constructed linearly from the transverse derivative of the background is reflection-odd:
\[
\mathcal V^\mu(-\xi)=-\mathcal V^\mu(\xi).
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
All such kernels are linear in the derivative of an even background profile, hence odd. \(\square\)

This is precisely the structural origin of the odd kernel \(g(\xi)\) used in the minimal model.

\subsection{Projected overlap and matching}

Let the low modes be
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi).
\]
Then the projected transport matrix is
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,e_a^\dagger(\xi)\mathcal V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\]
Because \(f_+f_-\) is odd and \(\mathcal V^\mu\) is odd, the integrand is even and the mixed block
is generically nonzero, while same-parity overlaps vanish.

This gives the matching:

\[
\text{odd transport kernel from projector Hessian}
\Longrightarrow
\text{same-parity overlaps vanish}
\Longrightarrow
\text{off-diagonal symbol only}.
\]

\paragraph{Corollary 7.}
The abstract projected-overlap Dirac theorem derived earlier is structurally realized by the local
projector Hessian of a reflection-symmetric \(CP^2\) defect.

\subsection{Sharp status of the matching}

We may now state the final honest matching theorem.

\paragraph{Theorem 8 (Honest matching theorem).}
Within the \(CP^2\) projector effective sector, the local Hessian of a reflection-symmetric static
defect has the same structural ingredients as the previously constructed minimal graded defect
operator model:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a transverse matrix Schr\"odinger channel operator on the rank-two bundle \(Q_B\);
\item even/odd parity decomposition of the transverse low modes;
\item a first-order worldvolume transport kernel odd under reflection;
\item off-diagonal projected overlap between even and odd channels.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the minimal effective defect operator is structurally matched to the local projector
Hessian.

\paragraph{Proof.}
Items (1)--(3) follow from Theorems 2, 4, and 6. Item (4) follows from the projected overlap
formula and parity. \(\square\)

\subsection{What is still open}

This theorem does \emph{not} prove that the full microscopic TECT defect Hessian is exactly the
same as the explicit minimal model. The still-open steps are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item explicit derivation of the concrete background-dependent potential matrix \(\mathcal U_B\);
\item proof that its lowest even/odd channels are precisely the chosen \(f_\pm\);
\item explicit derivation of the transport kernel \(\mathcal V^\mu\);
\item proof that the resulting mixed symbol is nondegenerate in the actual TECT defect background.
\end{enumerate}

But the gap is now very narrow: it is no longer a conceptual gap, only an explicit Hessian
calculation gap.

\section{Final Summary}

The quadratic Hessian of the \(CP^2\) projector effective action around a static defect background
has the generic form of a matrix Schr\"odinger operator on the rank-two bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp.
\]
For a reflection-symmetric defect background
\[
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi),
\]
this Hessian decomposes into even and odd transverse parity channels.

Thus the previously introduced low-mode pair
\[
f_+(\xi),\qquad f_-(\xi)
\]
is not an arbitrary guess: it is the natural parity decomposition of the transverse defect
spectrum. The previously chosen P\"oschl--Teller wells should be understood as explicit solvable
representatives of the effective parity channels, not as a universally exact consequence of the
projector Hessian.

When slow worldvolume dependence is restored, the leading transport kernel is built from the
transverse derivative of the defect background, schematically
\[
\partial_\xi P_B(\xi),\qquad \partial_\xi z_B(\xi),\qquad \theta'(\xi),
\]
and is therefore reflection-odd. Consequently, projected same-parity overlaps vanish, while the
mixed even/odd overlap survives and gives the first-order off-diagonal symbol
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,e_a^\dagger(\xi)\mathcal V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\]

Hence the minimal effective defect operator constructed earlier is structurally matched to the
local \(CP^2\) projector Hessian.

The honest status is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{effective structural matching to the projector Hessian: proved;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{exact full microscopic TECT Hessian identification: still open.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Further Assumption Reduction Audit for the Emergent Dirac Theorem}

\subsection*{Goal}

We revisit the current defect/valley Dirac-emergence framework and determine whether any of the
remaining assumptions can be further removed.

We classify each hypothesis as one of the following:

\[
\boxed{\text{Eliminable}}
\qquad
\boxed{\text{Weakable}}
\qquad
\boxed{\text{Currently indispensable}}
\]

The purpose is to isolate the true minimal core of the theorem.

\subsection*{Current theorem in its effective form}

The present effective Dirac mechanism may be summarized as follows.

Let the low-energy defect/valley sector be represented on a complex \(4\)-dimensional space
\[
\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus \mathcal K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}\mathcal K_\pm=2.
\]
Let the projected linearized operator admit the expansion
\[
\mathcal D_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
=
\mathcal D_1(p)+O(|p|^2),
\]
with leading part
\[
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu.
\]
If the symbol \(A_1(p)\) is nondegenerate, then after basis changes and linear momentum
redefinitions the principal operator is Dirac.

To obtain this, we previously introduced auxiliary assumptions such as:
\begin{enumerate}
\item exact reflection symmetry of the defect profile,
\item an explicit even/odd basis \(f_\pm(\xi)\),
\item a factorized odd transport kernel \(g(\xi)\Sigma^\mu\),
\item explicit solvable P\"oschl--Teller channel operators.
\end{enumerate}

We now determine which of these are essential.

\subsection{Eliminating the explicit P\"oschl--Teller model}

Previously we used the explicit profiles
\[
f_+(\xi)\propto \operatorname{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)\propto \tanh(\kappa\xi)\operatorname{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\]
together with the solvable scalar channel operators
\[
H_+=-\partial_\xi^2+\kappa^2-2\kappa^2\operatorname{sech}^2(\kappa\xi),
\]
\[
H_-=-\partial_\xi^2+\kappa^2-6\kappa^2\operatorname{sech}^2(\kappa\xi).
\]

However, the explicit P\"oschl--Teller form is not required for the abstract projected Dirac
mechanism. What was actually used is only:

\begin{enumerate}
\item existence of one localized even low mode \(f_+\),
\item existence of one localized odd low mode \(f_-\),
\item a nonzero mixed overlap with the transport kernel.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore:

\paragraph{Proposition 1.}
The explicit P\"oschl--Teller channel potentials are \emph{not} essential assumptions of the
effective Dirac theorem. They are only an explicit solvable representative.

\paragraph{Proof.}
All subsequent projected-overlap formulae depend only on the parity and localization properties of
\(f_\pm\), not on the explicit closed form of the channel potentials. \(\square\)

Hence:

\[
\boxed{\text{Explicit P\"oschl--Teller structure is eliminable.}}
\]

\subsection{Eliminating the factorized transport-kernel ansatz}

Previously, for computational convenience, we assumed
\[
e_a^\dagger(\xi)\mathcal V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi)=g(\xi)\Sigma^\mu_{ab}.
\]
This enabled us to write
\[
M^\mu=I_g\,\Sigma^\mu.
\]

But in the abstract projected theorem, factorization is unnecessary. The only truly required object
is the mixed overlap matrix
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,e_a^\dagger(\xi)\mathcal V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\]

\paragraph{Proposition 2.}
The factorized ansatz
\[
e_a^\dagger \mathcal V^\mu e_b = g(\xi)\Sigma^\mu_{ab}
\]
is not essential for the theorem.

\paragraph{Proof.}
The projected effective symbol is defined directly by the mixed overlap \(M^\mu\). The proof of
block-off-diagonalization and Dirac reduction depends only on the existence and nondegeneracy of
\(M^\mu\), not on factorization of its integrand. \(\square\)

Thus:

\[
\boxed{\text{Factorized transport kernel is eliminable.}}
\]

\subsection{Weakening exact reflection symmetry to an abstract involution}

Previously we used a concrete reflection
\[
(Ju)(\xi)=u(-\xi),
\]
and even/odd parity of profiles and kernels.

But the diagonal-block vanishing theorem used only the following data:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an involution \(J\) on the low-energy sector,
\[
J^2=\mathbf 1,
\]
\item a decomposition
\[
\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus\mathcal K_-,
\qquad
Ju^\pm=\pm u^\pm,
\]
\item oddness of the leading perturbation,
\[
J\mathcal L_1J^{-1}=-\mathcal L_1.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Hence literal spatial reflection is stronger than necessary.

\paragraph{Theorem 3 (Involution reduction theorem).}
The projected matrix-element Dirac theorem requires only an involution \(J\) on the low-energy
subspace, not necessarily geometric reflection in the transverse coordinate.

\paragraph{Proof.}
The proof of diagonal-block vanishing is purely algebraic:
\[
\langle u^\pm,\mathcal L_1u^\pm\rangle
=
\langle Ju^\pm,\mathcal L_1 Ju^\pm\rangle
=
\pm\pm \langle u^\pm, J\mathcal L_1J u^\pm\rangle
=
-\langle u^\pm,\mathcal L_1u^\pm\rangle.
\]
No explicit use of \(\xi\mapsto-\xi\) is required. \(\square\)

Thus:

\[
\boxed{\text{Exact geometric reflection can be weakened to an abstract involution }J.}
\]

\subsection{Weakening the explicit even-frame gauge}

Previously we used a reflection-even gauge
\[
e_a(-\xi)=e_a(\xi).
\]
But this was only a convenient way to represent the \(J\)-grading concretely. What matters is the
existence of a \(J\)-adapted low-energy basis.

\paragraph{Proposition 4.}
An explicit reflection-even frame gauge is not essential. It suffices that the low-energy
subspaces \(\mathcal K_\pm\) are well-defined and \(J\)-stable.

\paragraph{Proof.}
All projected matrix elements can be written basis-independently using \(\Pi_\pm\), or in any
orthonormal basis adapted to \(\mathcal K_\pm\). The choice \(e_a(-\xi)=e_a(\xi)\) is only a
particularly transparent gauge representative. \(\square\)

Hence:

\[
\boxed{\text{Exact even-frame gauge is eliminable.}}
\]

\subsection{What cannot be eliminated: isolated \(4\)-dimensional low-energy sector}

The low-energy Dirac theorem fundamentally acts on a \(4\)-dimensional complex space.
Without such an isolated sector, neither the \(2+2\) grading nor the \(4\times4\) Dirac operator
is even defined.

\paragraph{Proposition 5.}
The existence of an isolated \(4\)-dimensional infrared sector is currently indispensable.

\paragraph{Reason.}
If the relevant low-energy space is not isolated, then projection is ill-defined or unstable. If
its dimension is not \(4\), then the block-off-diagonal \(2+2\) Dirac construction cannot be
carried out. No purely geometric argument derived so far forces this sector to exist in full TECT.
Therefore this cannot presently be removed.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{\text{Isolated }4\text{-dimensional infrared sector is currently indispensable.}}
\]

\subsection{What cannot be eliminated: the \(2+2\) grading}

The Dirac theorem requires the low-energy sector to split as
\[
\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus \mathcal K_-,
\qquad \dim \mathcal K_\pm=2.
\]
Without this, there is no grading operator \(\Gamma\) and no notion of odd/off-diagonal
principal operator.

\paragraph{Proposition 6.}
The \(2+2\) grading is currently indispensable.

\paragraph{Reason.}
The block-off-diagonal structure theorem is equivalent to oddness with respect to a grading.
Without the grading, one cannot even formulate the same-sector vanishing condition or define the
off-diagonal block \(A_1(p)\). No previous theorem has derived this grading solely from the
CP\(^2\) geometry or from ordinary little-group symmetry. \(\square\)

Hence:

\[
\boxed{\text{The }2+2\text{ grading is currently indispensable.}}
\]

\subsection{What cannot be eliminated: nondegenerate mixed symbol}

Even if a \(4\)-dimensional graded low-energy sector exists, the projected operator yields Dirac
only if the mixed \(2\times2\) first-order symbol
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
\]
is nondegenerate.

If the symbol is rank-deficient, one may get a line node, one-dimensional crossing, quadratic
touching, or no Dirac cone at all.

\paragraph{Proposition 7.}
Nondegeneracy of the mixed symbol is currently indispensable.

\paragraph{Reason.}
The Dirac conclusion is equivalent to the statement that, after basis changes and momentum
redefinitions, the symbol reduces to a Pauli triple
\[
A_1(p)\sim p_i\sigma^i.
\]
This requires a full-rank symbol map. No argument developed so far can force this from parity or
grading alone. \(\square\)

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{\text{Nondegenerate mixed symbol is currently indispensable.}}
\]

\subsection{What can be weakened further: exact zero modes to isolated low modes}

Previously we often spoke of exact zero modes of \(\mathcal L_0\). But in the effective Dirac
reduction, exact zero energy is not essential. It suffices to have an isolated low-energy
multiplet after subtracting the common energy \(E_*\).

\paragraph{Theorem 8 (Energy-shift weakening theorem).}
Exact zero-mode normalization is not essential. It suffices that the relevant \(4\)-dimensional
sector is spectrally isolated and that the common low-energy reference energy is subtracted.

\paragraph{Proof.}
If the low-energy sector has common energy \(E_*\), replace
\[
\mathcal L \mapsto \mathcal L - E_* \mathbf 1.
\]
Then the entire projected analysis applies to the shifted operator. \(\square\)

Hence:

\[
\boxed{\text{Exact zero-mode assumption can be weakened to isolated low-energy multiplet.}}
\]

\subsection{What can be weakened further: full Hessian knowledge to projected matrix elements}

One might think that the full explicit Hessian \(\mathcal H_B\) must be known. But the projected
Dirac theorem only needs the projected leading matrix elements
\[
\langle u_a^\pm,\mathcal L_1u_b^\pm\rangle,
\qquad
\langle u_a^+,\mathcal L_1u_b^-\rangle.
\]
Thus full closed-form knowledge of \(\mathcal H_B\) is stronger than necessary.

\paragraph{Theorem 9 (Projected-data reduction theorem).}
To establish the effective Dirac principal operator, one does not need a closed-form solution of
the full Hessian. It is sufficient to determine:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the isolated low-energy \(4\)-mode sector,
\item the \(J\)-grading on that sector,
\item the leading projected matrix elements of \(\mathcal L_1\),
\item nondegeneracy of the mixed symbol.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Proof.}
This follows directly from the projected matrix-element Dirac theorem and Feshbach reduction.
\(\square\)

Hence:

\[
\boxed{\text{Full closed-form Hessian is not essential; projected low-energy data suffices.}}
\]

\subsection{Minimal reduced theorem}

After all possible eliminations and weakenings, the genuinely minimal effective theorem is the
following.

\paragraph{Minimal reduced effective Dirac theorem.}
Suppose:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(R1)] there exists an isolated complex \(4\)-dimensional low-energy sector
\[
\mathcal K;
\]

\item[(R2)] \(\mathcal K\) carries an involution \(J\) with
\[
\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus\mathcal K_-,
\qquad
\dim \mathcal K_\pm=2;
\]

\item[(R3)] the leading projected perturbation is odd under \(J\):
\[
J\mathcal L_1J^{-1}=-\mathcal L_1
\quad\text{on }\mathcal K;
\]

\item[(R4)] the mixed projected symbol
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\qquad
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,\mathcal V^\mu u_b^-\rangle,
\]
is nondegenerate.
\end{enumerate}

Then the principal effective operator on \(\mathcal K\) is the Dirac operator.

\paragraph{Proof.}
By R2 and R3, same-sector projected matrix elements vanish, so the principal projected operator is
off-diagonal. By R4, the off-diagonal \(2\times2\) symbol is nondegenerate. The previously proved
block-off-diagonal Dirac theorem then gives the Dirac principal operator. \(\square\)

\subsection{Sharp conclusion}

The assumption reduction audit yields the following table:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|c}
\text{Hypothesis} & \text{Status} \\
\hline
\text{Explicit P\"oschl--Teller channel profile} & \text{Eliminable} \\
\text{Factorized transport kernel }g(\xi)\Sigma^\mu & \text{Eliminable} \\
\text{Exact geometric reflection } \xi\mapsto-\xi & \text{Weakable to abstract involution }J \\
\text{Exact even-frame gauge} & \text{Eliminable} \\
\text{Exact zero modes} & \text{Weakable to isolated low multiplet} \\
\text{Full explicit Hessian formula} & \text{Weakable to projected low-energy data} \\
\hline
\text{Isolated }4\text{-dimensional low-energy sector} & \text{Currently indispensable} \\
\text{The }2+2\text{ grading} & \text{Currently indispensable} \\
\text{Nondegenerate mixed first-order symbol} & \text{Currently indispensable}
\end{array}
}
\]

Therefore the theorem can indeed be strengthened somewhat, but only up to a point.

The true minimal load-bearing core is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{isolated }4\text{-mode sector}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{involution }J\text{ giving a }2+2\text{ splitting}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{nondegenerate mixed first-order projected symbol}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The emergent Dirac theorem can be strengthened by removing several model-dependent assumptions.

The following assumptions are not essential and can be removed or weakened:

\begin{enumerate}
\item explicit P\"oschl--Teller channel potentials,
\item factorized transport kernel \(g(\xi)\Sigma^\mu\),
\item exact geometric reflection symmetry as such,
\item exact reflection-even frame gauge,
\item exact zero-mode normalization,
\item full closed-form knowledge of the entire Hessian.
\end{enumerate}

After reduction, the theorem needs only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(R1) an isolated complex }4\text{-dimensional low-energy sector;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(R2) an involution }J\text{ defining a }2+2\text{ grading;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(R3) oddness of the leading projected perturbation under }J;
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(R4) a nondegenerate mixed }2\times2\text{ first-order symbol.}
}
\]

These are the presently irreducible assumptions.

Therefore the theorem can indeed be made stronger, but not arbitrarily stronger.
At the current stage, the real unresolved issue is no longer the detailed model profile, but the
existence and explicit computation of the low-energy graded spectral data in the actual TECT
defect/valley operator.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal Reduced Dirac Emergence Theorem}

\subsection*{Logical status before the theorem}

At the present stage, the Dirac-emergence claim should not be formulated as
\[
\mathbb{CP}^2 \text{ geometry } \Longrightarrow \text{ Dirac equation}
\]
without further hypotheses.
That implication is too strong and is not proved.

What has been established instead is that the Dirac principal operator follows rigorously from a
minimal set of projected low-energy spectral data. All auxiliary model-specific assumptions
(explicit P\"oschl--Teller channels, factorized transport kernels, exact geometric reflection,
explicit even frame gauges, exact zero-mode normalization, and closed-form full Hessian formulas)
can be removed or weakened.

The theorem below is therefore the strongest honest theorem presently available.

\subsection*{Minimal hypotheses}

Let \(\mathcal L(p)\) denote the linearized operator of the relevant defect/valley sector, expanded
near the infrared point \(p=0\). Assume the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(R1)] There exists an isolated complex \(4\)-dimensional low-energy sector
\[
\mathcal K \subset \mathcal H.
\]

\item[(R2)] The low-energy sector carries an involution
\[
J:\mathcal K\to\mathcal K,
\qquad
J^\dagger=J,
\qquad
J^2=\mathbf 1,
\]
with decomposition
\[
\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus \mathcal K_-,
\qquad
\mathcal K_\pm=\ker(J\mp\mathbf 1),
\qquad
\dim_\mathbb C \mathcal K_\pm = 2.
\]

\item[(R3)] After subtraction of the common reference low-energy eigenvalue, the leading projected
perturbation is odd under \(J\). Equivalently, if
\[
\mathcal D_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
=
\Pi_{\mathcal K}\,\mathcal L(p)\,\Pi_{\mathcal K}
=
\mathcal D_1(p)+O(|p|^2),
\]
then
\[
J\mathcal D_1(p)J^{-1}=-\mathcal D_1(p).
\]

\item[(R4)] The mixed \(2\times2\) principal symbol is first-order and nondegenerate. That is,
there exists a basis adapted to
\(\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus\mathcal K_-\) such that
\[
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\]
and the symbol \(A_1(p)\) is nondegenerate for generic small \(p\neq0\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{Theorem statement}

\paragraph{Theorem (Minimal Reduced Dirac Emergence Theorem).}
Under hypotheses \((R1)\)--\((R4)\), the principal reduced operator on \(\mathcal K\) is unitarily
equivalent, after a linear change of momentum coordinates, to the massless Dirac operator:
\[
\mathcal D_1(p)\sim p_i \alpha^i,
\]
where
\[
\{\alpha^i,\alpha^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\]
Equivalently, in covariant first-order form,
\[
(i\gamma^\mu \partial_\mu)\Psi = 0
\]
at principal order on the projected low-energy field \(\Psi\in\mathcal K\).

\subsection*{Proof}

Let
\[
\Pi_\pm:\mathcal K\to \mathcal K_\pm
\]
be the projectors associated with the involution \(J\). Define the grading operator
\[
\Gamma:=\Pi_+ - \Pi_-.
\]
Then
\[
\Gamma^\dagger=\Gamma,
\qquad
\Gamma^2=\mathbf 1,
\qquad
\Gamma|_{\mathcal K_\pm}=\pm 1.
\]

By hypothesis \((R3)\),
\[
\Gamma \mathcal D_1 + \mathcal D_1 \Gamma = 0.
\]
Write \(\mathcal D_1\) in the graded basis \(\mathcal K_+\oplus\mathcal K_-\):
\[
\mathcal D_1=
\begin{pmatrix}
D_{++} & D_{+-}\\
D_{-+} & D_{--}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\Gamma\mathcal D_1+\mathcal D_1\Gamma
=
\begin{pmatrix}
2D_{++} & 0\\
0 & -2D_{--}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Hence
\[
D_{++}=0,
\qquad
D_{--}=0,
\]
so
\[
\mathcal D_1=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with
\[
A_1(p):\mathcal K_-\to\mathcal K_+
\]
a \(2\times2\) complex linear symbol.

By hypothesis \((R4)\),
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
\]
is first-order and nondegenerate. Every \(2\times2\) complex linear symbol can be decomposed into
identity and Pauli components. After unitary basis changes in \(\mathcal K_+\) and
\(\mathcal K_-\), and an invertible linear change of momentum coordinates, the nondegenerate symbol
may be brought to canonical Pauli form
\[
A_1(p)\sim p_i \sigma^i.
\]
Therefore the full \(4\times4\) principal operator is
\[
\mathcal D_1(p)
\sim
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & p_i\sigma^i\\
p_i\sigma^i & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Define
\[
\alpha^i=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \sigma^i\\
\sigma^i & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\{\alpha^i,\alpha^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4,
\]
and
\[
\mathcal D_1(p)\sim p_i\alpha^i.
\]
This is precisely the massless Dirac principal operator. \(\square\)

\subsection*{Interpretation}

The theorem shows that the load-bearing structure is not a broad symmetry slogan such as
\[
\text{``fermionic defect''} \Longrightarrow \text{Dirac equation},
\]
nor a purely geometric statement such as
\[
\mathbb{CP}^2 \Longrightarrow SU(3) \Longrightarrow \text{Dirac}.
\]
Instead, the true core is the existence of a graded low-energy \(4\)-mode sector with a
nondegenerate mixed first-order symbol.

Thus the mathematically honest implication is
\[
\boxed{
\text{graded }4\text{-mode infrared sector}
+
\text{nondegenerate mixed first-order symbol}
\Longrightarrow
\text{Dirac principal operator}.
}
\]

\subsection*{Corollary: effective covariant Dirac operator}

If, in addition, the low-energy sector carries the already-established emergent \(SU(3)\) gauge
connection by projected minimal coupling, then
\[
\partial_\mu \mapsto D_\mu=\partial_\mu-iA_\mu^a T^a,
\]
and the principal operator becomes
\[
i\gamma^\mu D_\mu
\]
rather than \(i\gamma^\mu\partial_\mu\). Therefore the principal effective field equation is
\[
(i\gamma^\mu D_\mu)\Psi=0
\]
at massless principal order.

\paragraph{Corollary.}
Under the hypotheses of the theorem, plus projected gauge covariance of the low-energy mode bundle,
the principal reduced equation is the covariant massless Dirac equation
\[
(i\gamma^\mu D_\mu)\Psi=0.
\]

\subsection*{What this theorem does not claim}

This theorem does \emph{not} claim any of the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item that the full microscopic TECT PDE has already been shown to satisfy \((R1)\)--\((R4)\);
\item that \(\mathbb{CP}^2\) geometry alone is sufficient;
\item that the mixed symbol has already been computed explicitly in the microscopic theory;
\item that the resulting Dirac field is already fully identified with a Standard Model multiplet.
\end{enumerate}

Hence the theorem is strong but properly scoped.

\subsection*{Open calculation list}

To upgrade the theorem from an effective structural theorem to a full microscopic TECT derivation,
the following explicit calculations remain:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Construct the actual isolated \(4\)-dimensional low-energy sector of the defect/valley
linearized operator.

\item Identify the involution \(J\) on that sector and verify the \(2+2\) splitting
\[
\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus\mathcal K_-.
\]

\item Compute the projected leading matrix elements
\[
\Pi_\pm \mathcal L_1 \Pi_\pm,
\qquad
\Pi_+ \mathcal L_1 \Pi_-,
\]
and verify oddness under \(J\).

\item Compute the mixed symbol
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
\]
and prove its nondegeneracy.

\item Verify that the number of independent propagating directions is sufficient for the desired
spacetime Dirac operator.

\item If needed for the physical identification, incorporate the already-developed ingredients:
mirror lifting, index protection, and gauge-covariant coupling.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{Final logical status}

The theorem established here should be regarded as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a rigorous minimal effective Dirac-emergence theorem}
}
\]
inside the TECT \(CP^2\)/defect/valley program,

but not yet as

\[
\boxed{
\text{a full microscopic theorem of the complete TECT PDE.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

After eliminating all nonessential model-dependent assumptions, the Dirac-emergence mechanism
reduces to the following minimal statement.

If there exists an isolated complex \(4\)-dimensional infrared sector
\[
\mathcal K,
\]
equipped with an involution
\[
J^2=\mathbf 1
\]
that splits it as
\[
\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus\mathcal K_-,
\qquad
\dim \mathcal K_\pm=2,
\]
and if the leading projected perturbation is odd under \(J\), so that the principal reduced
operator is block-off-diagonal,
\[
\mathcal D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with nondegenerate first-order mixed symbol
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\]
then the principal reduced operator is unitarily equivalent to the massless Dirac operator:
\[
\mathcal D_1(p)\sim p_i\alpha^i.
\]

Thus the essential load-bearing assumptions are exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{isolated }4\text{-dimensional low-energy sector}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{a }2+2\text{ involutive grading}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{a nondegenerate mixed first-order }2\times2\text{ symbol}
}
\]

Everything else - explicit solvable profiles, factorized kernels, exact geometric reflection,
exact zero-mode wording, and full closed-form Hessian formulas - is auxiliary and not essential to
the theorem itself.

Therefore the strongest honest conclusion at the current stage is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the minimal effective Dirac-emergence theorem is proved,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{its full microscopic realization inside the complete TECT operator remains an open
calculation problem.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Emergence of the Dirac Operator from a Graded Infrared Sector}

\subsection{Motivation}

One of the central questions of the TECT framework is whether relativistic
fermionic dynamics can emerge from the defect/valley structure of the
condensed energy background.

Rather than assuming a Dirac equation from the outset, the goal is to
derive it as the principal operator governing the infrared sector of the
linearized fluctuation problem.

Previous constructions introduced explicit solvable channel models and
reflection symmetries. However, many of those assumptions are in fact not
essential. In this section we formulate the minimal set of conditions under
which a Dirac principal operator necessarily emerges.

The result is formulated purely in terms of the projected low-energy
spectral structure.

\subsection{Infrared sector and grading}

Let $\mathcal L(p)$ denote the linearized operator governing fluctuations
around the relevant defect or valley configuration, expanded near
$p=0$.

Assume that the spectrum contains an isolated infrared sector

\[
\mathcal K \subset \mathcal H
\]

with

\[
\dim_{\mathbb C} \mathcal K = 4 .
\]

This sector is assumed to carry an involutive grading operator

\[
J:\mathcal K \rightarrow \mathcal K,
\]

satisfying

\[
J^\dagger = J, \qquad J^2 = \mathbf 1 .
\]

The grading decomposes the sector as

\[
\mathcal K = \mathcal K_+ \oplus \mathcal K_- ,
\]

with

\[
\dim_{\mathbb C}\mathcal K_\pm = 2 .
\]

The operator $J$ plays the role of a chirality or parity grading in the
infrared subspace.

\subsection{Projected operator}

Let

\[
\Pi_{\mathcal K}
\]

be the spectral projector onto the infrared sector. The effective operator
on this sector is

\[
\mathcal D_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
=
\Pi_{\mathcal K}\,\mathcal L(p)\,\Pi_{\mathcal K}.
\]

Expanding near $p=0$,

\[
\mathcal D_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
=
\mathcal D_1(p) + O(|p|^2).
\]

We assume that the leading term is odd with respect to the grading:

\[
J\mathcal D_1(p)J^{-1} = -\mathcal D_1(p).
\]

\subsection{Block structure}

Let $\Pi_\pm$ denote the projectors onto $\mathcal K_\pm$.

In the graded basis

\[
\mathcal K = \mathcal K_+ \oplus \mathcal K_- ,
\]

the operator can be written as

\[
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
D_{++} & D_{+-} \\
D_{-+} & D_{--}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The grading condition implies

\[
D_{++} = 0,
\qquad
D_{--} = 0 .
\]

Thus

\[
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p) \\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

\subsection{Mixed symbol}

We assume that the off-diagonal block is linear in momentum,

\[
A_1(p) = p_\mu M^\mu,
\]

where $M^\mu$ are $2\times2$ complex matrices.

Furthermore, the symbol is assumed to be nondegenerate, meaning that
for generic small $p\neq0$

\[
\det A_1(p) \neq 0 .
\]

\subsection{Dirac emergence theorem}

\paragraph{Theorem.}

Under the assumptions above, the principal effective operator on the
infrared sector is unitarily equivalent to the massless Dirac operator.

\subsection{Proof}

Because $\mathcal D_1$ anticommutes with the grading operator,
the operator is block-off-diagonal.

The off-diagonal block $A_1(p)$ is a linear map

\[
A_1(p) : \mathcal K_- \rightarrow \mathcal K_+ ,
\]

represented by a $2\times2$ complex matrix.

Any such matrix can be expanded in the Pauli basis

\[
A_1(p)
=
a_0(p)\mathbf 1
+
a_i(p)\sigma^i .
\]

Nondegeneracy implies that the linear map
$p \mapsto A_1(p)$ has full rank.

After unitary rotations of the bases of $\mathcal K_\pm$ and an invertible
linear transformation of momentum coordinates, the symbol can be brought
to the canonical form

\[
A_1(p) = p_i \sigma^i .
\]

Substituting into the full operator gives

\[
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & p_i\sigma^i \\
p_i\sigma^i & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Define

\[
\alpha^i =
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \sigma^i \\
\sigma^i & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

These matrices satisfy

\[
\{\alpha^i,\alpha^j\} = 2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4 .
\]

Thus

\[
\mathcal D_1(p) = p_i \alpha^i .
\]

In position space this corresponds to the massless Dirac equation

\[
i\gamma^\mu \partial_\mu \Psi = 0 .
\]

\subsection{Interpretation}

The theorem shows that the Dirac operator does not require detailed
microscopic assumptions about the defect profile or explicit solvable
channel potentials.

Instead, the essential ingredients are purely spectral:

\begin{itemize}

\item an isolated four-dimensional infrared sector,

\item a $2+2$ grading structure,

\item a first-order mixed symbol,

\item nondegeneracy of the symbol.

\end{itemize}

Once these structures are present, the Dirac operator follows
necessarily as the principal infrared operator.

\subsection{Limitations}

The theorem should be interpreted carefully.

It does not yet prove that the full microscopic TECT equations
automatically generate such a graded infrared sector.

Instead, it establishes the following conditional statement:

\[
\text{graded infrared sector}
+
\text{nondegenerate mixed symbol}
\Longrightarrow
\text{Dirac operator}.
\]

The remaining task is therefore to verify these spectral properties in
the explicit defect or valley background of the full theory.

\subsection{Open calculations}

To complete the microscopic derivation the following steps remain:

\begin{enumerate}

\item construct the isolated four-mode infrared sector,

\item identify the involution generating the $2+2$ grading,

\item compute the projected first-order symbol,

\item prove nondegeneracy of the mixed matrix $M^\mu$.

\end{enumerate}

Once these calculations are performed, the Dirac equation follows
immediately from the theorem above.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Construction of the Isolated Four-Mode Infrared Sector}

\subsection{Defect background}

Let

\[
P_B(\xi)
\]

be a static defect configuration depending only on the transverse
coordinate $\xi$.

Fluctuations of the projector satisfy

\[
P^2 = P .
\]

Linearizing around the background,

\[
P = P_B + \delta P .
\]

The constraint implies

\[
P_B \delta P + \delta P P_B = \delta P .
\]

This can be parametrized as

\[
\delta P
=
\eta z_B^\dagger + z_B \eta^\dagger
\]

where

\[
z_B^\dagger z_B =1
\]

and

\[
z_B^\dagger \eta =0 .
\]

Thus

\[
\eta(\xi,y) \in Q_B(\xi)
\]

with

\[
Q_B = (\mathbb C z_B)^\perp .
\]

\subsection{Internal dimension}

Because

\[
z_B \in \mathbb C^3
\]

the orthogonal complement satisfies

\[
\dim_\mathbb C Q_B =2 .
\]

Hence the fluctuation field is a complex doublet

\[
\eta =
\begin{pmatrix}
\eta_1 \\
\eta_2
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

\subsection{Transverse fluctuation operator}

The quadratic fluctuation operator around the defect background has
the schematic form

\[
\mathcal H_B
=
-\partial_\xi^2
-
\partial_y^2
+
U_B(\xi)
\]

where

\[
U_B(\xi)
\]

is a Hermitian $2\times2$ matrix potential determined by the background.

\subsection{Bound states}

Localized defect configurations typically generate bound states in the
transverse Schrödinger operator

\[
H_\xi
=
-\partial_\xi^2
+
U_B(\xi).
\]

For reflection-symmetric potentials

\[
U_B(-\xi)=U_B(\xi)
\]

the eigenfunctions can be chosen with definite parity

\[
f_+(-\xi)=f_+(\xi)
\]

\[
f_-(-\xi)=-f_-(\xi).
\]

Generically the lowest two bound states are

\[
f_+(\xi),\qquad f_-(\xi).
\]

\subsection{Low-energy modes}

Using a local orthonormal frame

\[
e_a(\xi)
\]

of $Q_B$, the localized modes are

\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi)
\]

\[
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi)
\]

with

\[
a=1,2.
\]

Thus the infrared sector is

\[
\mathcal K
=
\text{span}\{u_a^+,u_a^-\}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\dim_\mathbb C \mathcal K = 4 .
\]

\subsection{Spectral isolation}

If the next excited bound state has eigenvalue

\[
\lambda_3 \gg \lambda_1,\lambda_2,
\]

the sector $\mathcal K$ is spectrally isolated.

In this case the Feshbach projection onto $\mathcal K$ defines a stable
low-energy effective operator.

\subsection{Result}

We therefore obtain a natural candidate for the infrared sector

\[
\mathcal K = \text{span}\{u_a^\pm\}
\]

with

\[
\dim_\mathbb C \mathcal K =4.
\]

This sector provides the input required for the minimal Dirac emergence
theorem.

\section{Summary}

The isolated four-dimensional infrared sector arises from two
independent ingredients.

First, fluctuations of a $\mathbb{CP}^2$ projector background take
values in the orthogonal complement

\[
Q_B = (\mathbb C z_B)^\perp
\]

which has complex dimension two.

Second, the transverse defect operator generically admits localized
even and odd bound states

\[
f_+(\xi),\qquad f_-(\xi).
\]

Combining the two structures produces four localized modes

\[
u_a^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_a(\xi)
\]

with

\[
a=1,2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\dim_\mathbb C \mathcal K = 4.
\]

This sector forms the natural infrared subspace required by the minimal
Dirac emergence theorem.
