in the first-shell condensate or its first derivatives has first-shell Fourier support. The actual
Dirac question is whether that support survives the shell projection into two independent internal
traceless matrices.

\subsection{First-shell Fourier support of the BCC condensate}

The BCC condensate is
\[
\phi_0(x)=\sum_{G\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}} A_G e^{iG\cdot x},
\qquad
A_{-G}=\overline{A_G}.
\]
Thus its Fourier support is exactly the first reciprocal shell:
\[
\mathrm{supp}\,\widehat{\phi_0}\subseteq S_{\mathrm{BCC}}.
\]

Since the BCC reciprocal shell is the cuboctahedral \(12\)-vector star, with resonance count
\(\Lambda_{\mathrm{BCC}}=540\), the first-shell structure is already fixed by the BCC selection
theory. 

\paragraph{Proposition 1.}
If
\[
\mathcal T(x)=c\,\phi_0(x),
\]
then
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T}(G)=c\,A_G,
\]
so \(\mathcal T\) has the same first-shell support as \(\phi_0\).

\paragraph{Proof.}
Immediate from linearity of the Fourier transform. \(\square\)

\subsection{First-shell Fourier support of first-derivative couplings}

Now consider a coefficient field linear in the first derivatives of the condensate:
\[
\mathcal T_j(x)=\sum_{m} C_{jm}\,\partial_m \phi_0(x),
\]
with constant coefficients \(C_{jm}\).

Because
\[
\partial_m \phi_0(x)=\sum_{G\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}} iG_m A_G e^{iG\cdot x},
\]
we obtain
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T_j}(G)=i\sum_m C_{jm} G_m A_G.
\]

\paragraph{Theorem 1 (First-shell support for linear derivative couplings).}
Any coefficient field linear in the first derivatives of the BCC condensate,
\[
\mathcal T_j(x)=\sum_m C_{jm}\,\partial_m\phi_0(x),
\]
has Fourier support contained in the first shell:
\[
\mathrm{supp}\,\widehat{\mathcal T_j}\subseteq S_{\mathrm{BCC}}.
\]
Its shell Fourier coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal T_j}(G_*)
=
i\Bigl(\sum_m C_{jm} G_{*,m}\Bigr)A_{G_*}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
Differentation multiplies each harmonic \(e^{iG\cdot x}\) by \(iG_m\) but does not change the
wavevector \(G\). Hence the support remains first-shell. \(\square\)

\paragraph{Important consequence.}
This proves first-shell support, but not automatic nonvanishing for every \(j\). Vanishing can still
occur if
\[
\sum_m C_{jm} G_{*,m}=0.
\]
Thus one needs a coefficient tensor \(C_{jm}\) whose action on \(G_*\) is nonzero in at least the
relevant shell-projected channels.

\subsection{Constant-envelope shell projection}

For the simplest shell ansatz,
\[
u_a(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}\xi_a,
\qquad
\Psi_{\pm,a}(x)=e^{\pm ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
the projected shell overlaps reduce to primitive-cell Fourier coefficients.

As shown previously, the constant Bragg mass is
\[
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2.
\]
If the scalar periodic potential is quadratic in the first-shell condensate,
\[
U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)\propto \phi_0(x)^2,
\]
then
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0
\]
by the first-shell quadratic selection rule, hence
\[
B_0=0.
\]

For an enriched shell coupling of the form
\[
\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}\mathcal T^\alpha(x)\,(-i\partial_{p_\alpha})\otimes s^\alpha,
\]
the projected matrices are
\[
W^\alpha=\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)\,s^\alpha
\]
under the constant-envelope ansatz.

\paragraph{Theorem 2 (Constant-envelope enriched shell formula).}
Let \(\mathcal T^\alpha(x)\) be scalar periodic coefficient fields multiplying two fixed internal
Pauli matrices \(s^\alpha\), \(\alpha=1,2\). Then
\[
\boxed{
W^\alpha=\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)\,s^\alpha.
}
\]
Hence the shell-level Dirac problem reduces to the two numbers
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^1}(G_*),\qquad \widehat{\mathcal T^2}(G_*).
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
This is the previously derived shell-overlap formula specialized to the constant-envelope basis.
\(\square\)

\subsection{Correct shell-level Dirac criterion in Fourier form}

Combining the above, we obtain the corrected criterion.

\paragraph{Theorem 3 (Corrected Fourier shell-Dirac criterion).}
Under the constant-envelope enriched shell ansatz, a shell-level massless Dirac operator emerges if:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(i)] the scalar Bragg mass vanishes,
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0;
\]

\item[(ii)] the longitudinal pair slope is nonzero,
\[
v_\parallel=\hat n\cdot \nabla h_0(k_*)\neq0;
\]

\item[(iii)] the two enriched coefficient fields \(\mathcal T^1,\mathcal T^2\) have nonzero
first-shell Fourier coefficients,
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^1}(G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal T^2}(G_*)\neq0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then
\[
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
\sim
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1
+
\widehat{\mathcal T^1}(G_*)\,p_1\,\tau^1\otimes s^1
+
\widehat{\mathcal T^2}(G_*)\,p_2\,\tau^1\otimes s^2.
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
Item (i) gives \(B_0=0\). Item (ii) gives the pair-diagonal \(\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1\) term.
Item (iii) gives two nonzero traceless Hermitian transverse matrices
\[
W^1=\widehat{\mathcal T^1}(G_*)s^1,
\qquad
W^2=\widehat{\mathcal T^2}(G_*)s^2,
\]
which automatically anticommute. Hence the principal shell Hamiltonian is Dirac. \(\square\)

\subsection{What is actually proved and what remains open}

What is proved:

\begin{enumerate}
\item any coupling linear in \(\phi_0\) or \(\partial\phi_0\) has first-shell Fourier support;
\item the dangerous scalar Bragg mass vanishes for quadratic first-shell scalar potentials;
\item the shell-level Dirac criterion reduces to nonvanishing of two shell-projected enriched
first-shell coefficients.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual microscopic TECT linearization has not yet been shown to produce the enriched
coefficient fields \(\mathcal T^1,\mathcal T^2\) with the required internal Pauli assignment;

\item even when first-shell support is present, accidental cancellations or symmetry constraints may
still force
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)=0
\]
for one or both \(\alpha\);

\item the enriched shell block must still be shown to be spectrally isolated.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the remaining shell-level problem is now a sharply defined Fourier bookkeeping and spectral
isolation problem.

\section{Final Summary}

The previous heuristic claim that
\[
\mathcal G_\alpha(x)=\lambda\,\partial_\alpha\phi_0(x)
\]
automatically implies the nonvanishing of both shell-level transverse Dirac couplings was too
strong and must be corrected.

What is rigorously true is the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the BCC condensate
\[
\phi_0(x)=\sum_{G\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}A_G e^{iG\cdot x}
\]
has support exactly on the first reciprocal shell;

\item any coefficient field linear in \(\phi_0\) or its first derivatives has Fourier support still
contained in that same first shell;

\item under the constant-envelope shell ansatz, the shell-level transverse matrices are
\[
W^\alpha=\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)\,s^\alpha,
\]
so the shell-level Dirac problem reduces to whether two enriched coefficient fields
\(\mathcal T^1,\mathcal T^2\) have nonzero \(G_*\)-Fourier coefficients;

\item the scalar Bragg mass still vanishes by the quadratic first-shell selection rule:
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the corrected shell-level Dirac criterion is

\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal T^1}(G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal T^2}(G_*)\neq0.
\]

The remaining microscopic task is thus sharply localized:
identify the actual enriched coefficient fields produced by the TECT linearization, compute their
\(G_*\)-Fourier coefficients, and prove shell-block isolation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Classification of Allowed Enriched Couplings for Shell-Level Dirac Emergence}

\subsection*{Goal}

The remaining shell-level Dirac conditions have been reduced to the nonvanishing of two
projected enriched Fourier coefficients:
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^1}(G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal T^2}(G_*)\neq0.
\]
We now classify the minimal allowed forms of the enriched coefficient fields
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x),
\qquad \alpha=1,2,
\]
and determine which classes can or cannot contribute at the first reciprocal shell.

\subsection*{Background}

The BCC condensate is
\[
\phi_0(x)=\sum_{G\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}A_G e^{iG\cdot x},
\qquad
A_{-G}=\overline{A_G},
\]
with support exactly on the first reciprocal shell:
\[
\mathrm{supp}\,\widehat{\phi_0}\subseteq S_{\mathrm{BCC}}.
\]
Thus any candidate enriched coefficient field built from \(\phi_0\) and finitely many derivatives
inherits Fourier support from the algebra of these first-shell harmonics.

The shell-level Dirac criterion in the constant-envelope ansatz takes the form
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal T^1}(G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal T^2}(G_*)\neq0.
\]
The scalar Bragg mass condition \(\widehat U(G_*)=0\) has already been controlled by a quadratic
first-shell selection rule. The present question is therefore entirely about the enriched
coefficient fields \(\mathcal T^\alpha\).

\subsection{General algebraic classification}

Let \(\mathfrak A[\phi_0]\) denote the algebra generated by \(\phi_0\) and its spatial derivatives.
A generic enriched coefficient field may be expanded as a finite sum of monomials in
\[
\phi_0,\qquad \partial_j\phi_0,\qquad \partial_j\partial_k\phi_0,\qquad \ldots
\]
with tensor coefficients.

For shell-level Dirac emergence, the lowest-order and most relevant possibilities are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(L0)] linear scalar coupling:
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=c^\alpha \phi_0(x);
\]

\item[(L1)] linear derivative coupling:
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x);
\]

\item[(Q0)] quadratic scalar coupling:
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=d^\alpha\,\phi_0(x)^2;
\]

\item[(Q1)] mixed quadratic derivative coupling:
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=D^\alpha{}_j\,\phi_0(x)\partial_j\phi_0(x);
\]

\item[(Q2)] quadratic gradient bilinear:
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=E^\alpha{}_{jk}\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\partial_k\phi_0(x).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Higher-order monomials may also be considered, but these are enough to establish the main shell
selection rules.

\subsection{Fourier-support rules}

We now determine the shell content of each class.

\paragraph{Proposition 1 (Linear shell-support rule).}
If \(\mathcal T^\alpha\) is linear in \(\phi_0\) or in its derivatives, then
\[
\mathrm{supp}\,\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}\subseteq S_{\mathrm{BCC}}.
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
For \(\mathcal T^\alpha\propto \phi_0\), the claim is immediate. For
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha=C^\alpha{}_j\partial_j\phi_0,
\]
differentiation multiplies each harmonic \(e^{iG\cdot x}\) by \(iG_j\) but does not change its
wavevector. Hence the support remains on the first shell. \(\square\)

Thus the linear classes (L0) and (L1) are favorable for shell-level Dirac emergence.

\paragraph{Proposition 2 (Quadratic shell-support rule).}
If \(\mathcal T^\alpha\) is quadratic in \(\phi_0\) and its first derivatives, then
\[
\mathrm{supp}\,\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}\subseteq S_{\mathrm{BCC}}+S_{\mathrm{BCC}}
=
\{G+G':G,G'\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\}.
\]
In particular, such quadratic classes generally do not automatically contain a single first-shell
vector \(G_*\).

\paragraph{Proof.}
Products of two first-shell harmonics produce wavevectors equal to sums of first-shell vectors.
Thus the support is contained in the Minkowski sum \(S_{\mathrm{BCC}}+S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\). \(\square\)

This is the same mechanism that killed the scalar Bragg mass in the quadratic potential:
a quadratic function of first-shell harmonics does not generically produce a single first-shell
wavevector.

Hence the quadratic classes (Q0)--(Q2) are generically unfavorable for producing
\(\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)\neq 0\).

\subsection{Consequences for shell-level Dirac}

We immediately obtain the first classification statement.

\paragraph{Theorem 1 (Allowed-coupling classification theorem).}
At the minimal shell level, the enriched couplings that can generically support the shell-Dirac
conditions
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^1}(G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal T^2}(G_*)\neq0
\]
must contain a component linear in the first-shell condensate \(\phi_0\) or its first derivatives.
Purely quadratic enriched couplings are generically insufficient.

\paragraph{Proof.}
By Propositions 1 and 2, only the linear classes are guaranteed to retain first-shell Fourier
support. Quadratic classes shift support to sums of shell vectors and therefore generally do not
produce nonzero \(G_*\)-Fourier coefficients. \(\square\)

\subsection{Refinement: when derivative couplings vanish}

We now analyze the most relevant class:
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x).
\]
Its shell Fourier coefficient is
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)
=
i\bigl(C^\alpha\cdot G_*\bigr)A_{G_*},
\]
where
\[
C^\alpha\cdot G_*:=\sum_j C^\alpha{}_j G_{*,j}.
\]

This gives a sharp criterion.

\paragraph{Theorem 2 (Derivative-coupling nonvanishing criterion).}
Suppose
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x).
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)\neq0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
(C^\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\neq0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
Immediate from the Fourier coefficient formula above. \(\square\)

\paragraph{Important consequence.}
This shows precisely why the naive choice
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha=\partial_\alpha\phi_0
\]
is not generally sufficient when \(\alpha\) labels directions transverse to \(G_*\): in that case
\[
G_{*,\alpha}=0
\]
may occur, forcing
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)=0.
\]

Therefore a generic shell-Dirac construction requires a more general tensorial coupling
\[
C^\alpha{}_j
\]
that mixes the shell-transverse labels \(\alpha=1,2\) with the actual spatial derivative index \(j\).

\subsection{Strong sufficient condition}

We can now state the most useful sufficient criterion.

\paragraph{Theorem 3 (Strong sufficient shell-coupling criterion).}
Suppose the enriched coefficient fields are
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x),
\qquad \alpha=1,2,
\]
and that
\[
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
C^1\cdot G_*\neq0,
\qquad
C^2\cdot G_*\neq0.
\]
Then
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^1}(G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal T^2}(G_*)\neq0.
\]
Under the constant-envelope shell ansatz, this implies
\[
W^1=\widehat{\mathcal T^1}(G_*)\,s^1\neq0,
\qquad
W^2=\widehat{\mathcal T^2}(G_*)\,s^2\neq0,
\]
and therefore the two transverse shell-Dirac matrices automatically anticommute.

\paragraph{Proof.}
By Theorem 2, the Fourier coefficients are nonzero whenever \(C^\alpha\cdot G_*\neq0\) and
\(A_{G_*}\neq0\). The shell-overlap formula then gives
\[
W^\alpha=\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)s^\alpha.
\]
Since \(s^1\) and \(s^2\) anticommute, so do \(W^1\) and \(W^2\). \(\square\)

\subsection{Symmetry-based obstructions}

It is equally important to identify what can kill the needed couplings.

\paragraph{Proposition 4 (Symmetry obstruction).}
If the enriched coefficient field \(\mathcal T^\alpha\) transforms under a symmetry in such a way
that its \(G_*\)-Fourier component is forbidden, then
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)=0.
\]
In particular, any symmetry forcing \(C^\alpha\cdot G_*=0\) kills the corresponding shell-Dirac
matrix \(W^\alpha\).

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
Thus one should not demand too strong a transverse-selection symmetry at the shell point, or the
desired Dirac couplings may be removed together with unwanted terms.

\subsection{Minimal microscopic target}

The classification above shows that the actual microscopic task is now very specific.

To prove shell-level Dirac emergence, it is sufficient to identify two enriched microscopic
coefficient fields \(\mathcal T^1,\mathcal T^2\) such that:

\begin{enumerate}
\item each contains a linear first-shell component,
\item neither has its \(G_*\)-Fourier coefficient removed by symmetry,
\item their shell projections are attached to two distinct internal Pauli directions.
\end{enumerate}

This leads to the final theorem of this step.

\paragraph{Theorem 5 (Minimal enriched-coupling target theorem).}
The remaining microscopic shell-level Dirac problem is reduced to the following finite question:

Find two enriched coefficient fields
\[
\mathcal T^1(x),\qquad \mathcal T^2(x),
\]
allowed by the microscopic TECT linearization, such that
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^1}(G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal T^2}(G_*)\neq0,
\]
and such that their shell projections couple to two independent traceless internal matrices.

Once this is achieved, the transverse shell-Dirac structure is established.

\paragraph{Proof.}
This is the direct content of Theorem 3 together with the previously established shell-projected
Dirac theorem. \(\square\)

\section{Final Summary}

The shell-level Dirac problem has now been reduced to a classification problem for the enriched
coefficient fields \(\mathcal T^\alpha(x)\).

The main conclusions are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item couplings linear in the first-shell condensate \(\phi_0\) or its first derivatives retain
first-shell Fourier support and are therefore viable candidates for shell-Dirac emergence;

\item purely quadratic enriched couplings are generically unfavorable, because they shift Fourier
support to sums of shell vectors and need not produce a nonzero \(G_*\)-harmonic;

\item for derivative-type enriched couplings
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x),
\]
the shell coefficient is explicitly
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)
=
i(C^\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*};
\]

\item therefore the shell-level transverse Dirac matrices are nonzero exactly when the coupling
tensors satisfy
\[
C^1\cdot G_*\neq0,
\qquad
C^2\cdot G_*\neq0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Thus the remaining microscopic problem is no longer vague. It is to identify two enriched
microscopic coefficient fields allowed by the TECT linearization whose \(G_*\)-Fourier coefficients
survive projection and couple to two independent internal traceless matrices.

This is the sharpest currently honest formulation of the remaining shell-level Dirac task.

%%%%%%%

\section{Symmetry Classification of Allowed Enriched Couplings for Shell-Level Dirac Emergence}

\subsection*{Goal}

The remaining shell-level Dirac condition has been reduced to the existence of two enriched
coefficient fields
\[
\mathcal T^1(x),\qquad \mathcal T^2(x),
\]
whose shell Fourier coefficients survive at \(G_*\) and project to two independent traceless
internal matrices.

We now classify which forms of \(\mathcal T^\alpha(x)\) are allowed or forbidden by the relevant
symmetries.

\subsection{Data of the shell problem}

We assume the following ingredients are already fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a periodic BCC condensate
\[
\phi_0(x)=\sum_{G\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}} A_G e^{iG\cdot x};
\]

\item a chosen shell vector \(G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\) and Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2};
\]

\item an enriched shell space
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}};
\]

\item a shell Hamiltonian whose transverse part is controlled by two enriched coefficient fields
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x),\qquad \alpha=1,2.
\]
\end{enumerate}

The shell-level Dirac condition requires
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^1}(G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal T^2}(G_*)\neq 0,
\]
with their shell projections attached to two independent traceless Hermitian internal matrices.

\subsection{Relevant symmetries}

The relevant symmetries are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item lattice translation symmetry;
\item shell-exchange / Bragg reflection symmetry;
\item cubic point-group symmetry of the BCC reciprocal star;
\item internal \(U(1)\) or \(SU(2)\)-type symmetry acting on the internal doublet.
\end{enumerate}

We now analyze their consequences one by one.

\subsection{Translation symmetry}

Because the background is periodic, any allowed coefficient field must be periodic with the same
lattice:
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x+\mathbf R)=\mathcal T^\alpha(x).
\]
Hence \(\mathcal T^\alpha\) admits a reciprocal-lattice Fourier expansion
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=\sum_{G\in\mathcal G}\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G)e^{iG\cdot x}.
\]

\paragraph{Proposition 1 (Translation constraint).}
Translation symmetry does not forbid a shell-level Dirac coupling by itself. It only implies that
the coefficient fields are expanded in reciprocal-lattice harmonics, so the shell problem is
controlled by the single Fourier coefficient
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*).
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
This is the direct consequence of lattice periodicity and Bloch theory. \(\square\)

Thus translation symmetry is neutral with respect to shell-Dirac emergence: it localizes the
problem to a reciprocal-shell Fourier coefficient, but does not force it to vanish.

\subsection{Shell exchange and reflection symmetry}

Let the pair sector be spanned by the shell pair basis
\[
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x).
\]
The natural shell-exchange involution interchanges the two pair sectors:
\[
\mathsf J:\Psi_{+,a}\leftrightarrow \Psi_{-,a}.
\]

The shell Hamiltonian decomposes as
\[
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
The constant Bragg mass \(B_0=B(0)\) is even under momentum reversal and is the dangerous term that
gaps the shell crossing. The desired transverse Dirac couplings, by contrast, must be linear in the
small deviation \(p\) and are therefore odd under \(p\to -p\).

\paragraph{Proposition 2 (Reflection-parity separation).}
A shell symmetry that removes pair-even shell mixing at \(p=0\) can kill the constant Bragg mass
\(B_0\) while still allowing linear pair-mixing terms \(p_\alpha W^\alpha\), provided the
underlying enriched coefficient fields transform with the appropriate odd shell parity.

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
Thus shell reflection/exchange symmetry is favorable if it removes constant mixing but preserves
linear odd mixing. It becomes unfavorable only if imposed too strongly, in which case the linear
transverse terms may also be eliminated.

\subsection{Cubic symmetry and the transverse doublet}

Fix the shell direction
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\]
The tangent plane orthogonal to \(\hat n\) carries a natural \(2\)-dimensional transverse
representation. Let \(\alpha=1,2\) label a basis of this transverse plane.

The point-group symmetry preserving the shell direction acts on the transverse plane by a real
\(2\times2\) representation. Therefore the pair of coefficient fields
\[
(\mathcal T^1,\mathcal T^2)
\]
must transform as a transverse doublet.

\paragraph{Theorem 1 (Cubic-transverse representation constraint).}
For shell-level Dirac emergence, the enriched couplings must transform as a transverse doublet under
the little group of the shell direction \(G_*\). In particular, the most natural allowed linear
couplings are of the form
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j \phi_0(x),
\]
where \(C^\alpha{}_j\) is an intertwining tensor from the spatial vector representation to the
transverse-shell doublet.

\paragraph{Proof.}
The shell Hamiltonian requires two linearly independent transverse momentum directions
\(p_1,p_2\), so the coefficient fields must transform in the same \(2\)-dimensional transverse
representation. The only minimal linear spatial object available from the condensate is
\(\partial_j\phi_0\), hence the coefficient tensor \(C^\alpha{}_j\) is the minimal intertwiner.
\(\square\)

This identifies the most natural minimal shell-Dirac coupling.

\subsection{Internal symmetry}

Now consider the internal doublet sector \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\). The projected transverse
matrices must be traceless Hermitian and independent:
\[
W^1,\qquad W^2.
\]
To get Dirac, they must be reducible to two anticommuting Pauli generators. Therefore the internal
sector must allow at least two independent traceless Hermitian generators.

\paragraph{Theorem 2 (Minimal internal symmetry requirement).}
A necessary internal condition for shell-level Dirac emergence is that the internal low-energy
sector admit a complex doublet structure with at least two independent traceless Hermitian
generators. Equivalently, the internal sector must support a local \(SU(2)\)-type Pauli algebra.

\paragraph{Proof.}
The shell-level Dirac theorem requires two transverse matrices \(W^1,W^2\) satisfying
\[
\{W^1,W^2\}=0,
\qquad
(W^\alpha)^2\propto \mathbf 1.
\]
Such a pair exists if and only if the internal sector supports two independent traceless Hermitian
\(2\times2\) generators, i.e. a Pauli algebra. \(\square\)

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
A purely scalar internal sector cannot produce shell-level Dirac. The minimal internal carrier is a
complex doublet.

\subsection{Classification of allowed coupling types}

We now combine the Fourier-support analysis with the symmetry constraints.

\paragraph{Class A: linear scalar coupling}
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=c^\alpha \phi_0(x).
\]

\begin{itemize}
\item Fourier support: favorable (first shell survives).
\item Cubic-transverse structure: generally unfavorable, because this does not naturally transform
as a transverse doublet unless supplemented by an external tensor structure.
\item Internal structure: must still be attached to a nontrivial internal generator.
\end{itemize}

Thus this class is only conditionally useful.

\paragraph{Class B: linear derivative coupling}
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x).
\]

\begin{itemize}
\item Fourier support: favorable.
\item Little-group transformation: favorable; this is the natural transverse-doublet candidate.
\item Internal structure: favorable once attached to \(s^\alpha\).
\end{itemize}

This is the most natural minimal shell-Dirac coupling class.

\paragraph{Class C: quadratic scalar or gradient couplings}
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha\sim \phi_0^2,\qquad
\phi_0\partial\phi_0,\qquad
(\partial\phi_0)^2.
\]

\begin{itemize}
\item Fourier support: generally unfavorable for first-shell survival.
\item Shell-level Dirac: generically suppressed unless additional fine-tuned cancellations or
higher-order resonance effects restore the shell coefficient.
\end{itemize}

Thus purely quadratic enriched couplings are not minimal shell-Dirac candidates.

\paragraph{Theorem 3 (Allowed-coupling classification).}
Among low-order enriched coefficient fields built from the BCC condensate, the only generic minimal
class simultaneously compatible with shell Fourier support, transverse doublet structure, and
internal Pauli coupling is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha,
\qquad \alpha=1,2.
}
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
Linear derivative couplings retain first-shell support, transform naturally as spatial vectors, and
can be converted into transverse-doublet objects by the intertwiner \(C^\alpha{}_j\). When attached
to internal Pauli generators \(s^\alpha\), they produce the required independent traceless internal
matrices. The other low-order classes fail at least one of these requirements generically.
\(\square\)

\subsection{Nonvanishing criterion}

For the minimal allowed class,
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha,
\]
the shell Fourier coefficient is
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)
=
i(C^\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\,s^\alpha.
\]
Hence:

\paragraph{Theorem 4 (Nonvanishing criterion for the minimal allowed class).}
Suppose
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha.
\]
Then
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)\neq0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
(C^\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\neq0.
\]
Therefore shell-level Dirac emerges provided
\[
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
C^1\cdot G_*\neq0,
\qquad
C^2\cdot G_*\neq0,
\]
together with the already-established conditions
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq0.
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
This follows from the Fourier formula for derivative couplings together with the shell projection
formula \(W^\alpha=\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)\). \(\square\)

\subsection{Symmetry obstructions}

The same formula identifies the obstructions.

\paragraph{Proposition 5 (Obstruction table).}
The shell-Dirac transverse couplings are killed if any of the following hold:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the condensate amplitude vanishes at the selected shell:
\[
A_{G_*}=0;
\]

\item the tensor intertwiners satisfy
\[
C^\alpha\cdot G_*=0;
\]

\item an internal symmetry reduces the shell projection to fewer than two independent traceless
generators;

\item an accidental cancellation removes the \(G_*\)-harmonic in the enriched coefficient field.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
Thus the symmetry requirements must be balanced carefully: enough symmetry to control \(B_0\), but
not so much that all transverse shell couplings are forced to vanish.

\subsection{Minimal microscopic target}

We can now formulate the remaining microscopic task in its sharpest form.

\paragraph{Theorem 5 (Minimal microscopic target theorem).}
To close the shell-level Dirac problem, it is sufficient to identify in the TECT linearization two
allowed enriched coefficient fields of the form
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha,
\qquad \alpha=1,2,
\]
such that
\[
C^1\cdot G_*\neq0,
\qquad
C^2\cdot G_*\neq0,
\]
and such that the enriched shell block is spectrally isolated.

Once this is achieved, the shell-projected Hamiltonian is Dirac.

\paragraph{Proof.}
Theorem 4 gives the transverse Dirac couplings, while the earlier shell-level Dirac theorem uses
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0,\qquad v_\parallel\neq0
\]
to complete the Clifford triple. Spectral isolation ensures the validity of the shell projection.
\(\square\)

\section{Final Summary}

The shell-level Dirac problem is now reduced to a symmetry-classification problem for the enriched
coefficient fields \(\mathcal T^\alpha(x)\).

The main conclusions are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item translation symmetry only localizes the problem to the \(G_*\)-Fourier coefficient;

\item shell reflection/exchange symmetry is useful if it removes the constant Bragg mass \(B_0\)
without killing the linear transverse pair-mixing;

\item cubic symmetry implies that the transverse couplings must transform as a two-dimensional
transverse-shell doublet;

\item the internal sector must support at least two independent traceless Hermitian generators,
i.e. a local \(SU(2)\)-type Pauli algebra.
\end{enumerate}

Among low-order couplings, the generic minimal allowed class is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha,
\qquad \alpha=1,2.
}
\]

Its shell Fourier coefficient is

\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)
=
i(C^\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\,s^\alpha.
\]

Therefore the remaining microscopic shell-Dirac condition is simply

\[
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
C^1\cdot G_*\neq0,
\qquad
C^2\cdot G_*\neq0,
\]
together with the previously established conditions
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq0,
\]
and spectral isolation of the enriched shell block.

This is the sharpest currently honest formulation of the remaining shell-level Dirac task.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Microscopic Tensor Reduction Theorem for Shell-Transverse Enriched Couplings}

\subsection*{Goal}

The remaining shell-level Dirac condition was reduced to the existence of two enriched coefficient
fields of the form
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha,
\qquad \alpha=1,2.
\]
We now show how such fields arise from the most general gradient-linear microscopic tensor coupling,
once a shell direction is chosen and the spatial tensor structure is reduced to the transverse shell
doublet.

\subsection*{Logical status}

What is proved here is a \emph{reduction theorem}:
if the microscopic linearization contains a gradient-linear enriched tensor coupling, then its
shell-transverse projection necessarily takes the standard shell-Dirac form above.

What is \emph{not} proved automatically is that the relevant microscopic tensor coefficients are
nonzero or generic enough to satisfy the final nonvanishing conditions.

\subsection{General gradient-linear enriched coupling}

Let the microscopic or effective TECT linearization around the periodic condensate contain a
first-order enriched term of the schematic form
\[
\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
\mathsf M_{ij}^{A}\,
(\partial_i\phi_0(x))\,
(-i\partial_j)\otimes S_A,
\]
where:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(i,j=1,2,3\) are spatial indices;
\item \(A\) labels Hermitian generators acting on the internal low-energy sector;
\item \(\mathsf M_{ij}^{A}\) is a real microscopic tensor coefficient.
\end{enumerate}

Assume the internal low-energy sector reduces to a complex doublet, so that its traceless Hermitian
generators are spanned by Pauli matrices \(s^a\), \(a=1,2,3\). Then
\[
S_A = u_A\,\mathbf 1_2 + v_A^a\,s^a.
\]
Only the traceless part contributes to shell-level Dirac structure, so we discard the scalar part
and write the enriched term as
\[
\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
\mathsf N_{ij}^{a}\,
(\partial_i\phi_0(x))\,
(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\]

\paragraph{Proposition 1 (Internal Pauli reduction).}
Any gradient-linear enriched microscopic term on an internal complex doublet reduces uniquely to
\[
\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
\mathsf N_{ij}^{a}\,
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,
(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a
\]
up to an irrelevant internal scalar term proportional to \(\mathbf 1_2\).

\paragraph{Proof.}
The Hermitian \(2\times2\) operator algebra decomposes as
\[
\mathrm{Herm}(2)=\mathbb R\,\mathbf 1_2\oplus \mathrm{span}\{s^1,s^2,s^3\}.
\]
Projecting to the traceless part gives the claim. \(\square\)

\subsection{Choice of shell direction and transverse projector}

Fix a shell vector \(G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\), and define the unit shell direction
\[
\hat n_i=\frac{G_{*,i}}{|G_*|}.
\]
The orthogonal projector onto the shell-transverse plane is
\[
P^\perp_{ij}=\delta_{ij}-\hat n_i\hat n_j.
\]
Choose an orthonormal transverse basis
\[
e^\alpha_i,\qquad \alpha=1,2,
\]
satisfying
\[
e^\alpha_i \hat n_i=0,
\qquad
e^\alpha_i e^\beta_i=\delta^{\alpha\beta},
\qquad
P^\perp_{ij}=e^\alpha_i e^\alpha_j.
\]

Any spatial covector \(X_i\) decomposes as
\[
X_i = X_\parallel \hat n_i + X_\alpha e^\alpha_i,
\qquad
X_\parallel = \hat n_i X_i,
\qquad
X_\alpha = e^\alpha_i X_i.
\]

\subsection{Shell-transverse tensor reduction}

The shell-level transverse Dirac structure uses only the two transverse momentum directions
\[
p_\alpha = e^\alpha_j p_j.
\]
Accordingly, from the general microscopic tensor \(\mathsf N_{ij}^a\) we extract the shell-relevant
transverse coefficients by projecting the first spatial index onto the transverse basis:
\[
C^{\alpha a}{}_j := e^\alpha_i\,\mathsf N_{ij}^a.
\]
Then the enriched microscopic term becomes
\[
\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
C^{\alpha a}{}_j\,
\bigl(e^\alpha_i\partial_i\phi_0(x)\bigr)\,
(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a
+
(\text{longitudinal pieces}).
\]

Equivalently, after transverse reduction,
\[
\mathcal T^{\alpha a}(x)=C^{\alpha a}{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x).
\]

\paragraph{Theorem 1 (Microscopic tensor reduction theorem).}
Let
\[
\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
\mathsf N_{ij}^{a}\,
(\partial_i\phi_0(x))\,
(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a
\]
be a gradient-linear enriched coupling in the microscopic TECT linearization. Then, after choosing a
shell direction \(G_*\) and projecting to the shell-transverse plane, the shell-relevant enriched
coefficient fields necessarily take the form
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T^{\alpha a}(x)=C^{\alpha a}{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x),
\qquad
C^{\alpha a}{}_j=e^\alpha_i\,\mathsf N_{ij}^{a}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
This is just the decomposition of the first spatial index into transverse and longitudinal parts,
followed by restriction to the transverse shell doublet. \(\square\)

This proves that the previously introduced shell-level ansatz
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha
\]
is not ad hoc: it is exactly the canonical shell-transverse reduction of the most general
gradient-linear microscopic tensor coupling.

\subsection{Minimal shell-Dirac standard form}

The shell-level Dirac theorem needs two independent transverse internal directions. Hence we now
restrict to the minimal case where only two internal traceless directions survive:
\[
a=1,2.
\]
If, after internal basis choice, the microscopic tensor has the reduced form
\[
\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
\mathsf N_{ij}^{1}(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^1
+
\mathsf N_{ij}^{2}(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^2,
\]
then the shell-transverse reduction becomes
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha,
\qquad
C^\alpha{}_j=e^\alpha_i\,\mathsf N_{ij}^{\alpha},
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\]

\paragraph{Corollary 2 (Minimal standard shell form).}
Any microscopic enriched linearization whose traceless internal part has two independent Pauli
directions reduces, on the shell-transverse sector, to the standard minimal shell-Dirac coupling
form above.

\subsection{Fourier coefficient formula after tensor reduction}

Using the first-shell Fourier expansion
\[
\phi_0(x)=\sum_{G\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}A_G e^{iG\cdot x},
\]
we have
\[
\partial_j\phi_0(x)=\sum_{G\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}} iG_j A_G e^{iG\cdot x}.
\]
Therefore
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^{\alpha a}}(G_*)
=
i\,C^{\alpha a}{}_j\,G_{*,j}\,A_{G_*}.
\]

In the minimal standard form,
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)
=
i\,(C^\alpha\cdot G_*)\,A_{G_*}\,s^\alpha.
\]

\paragraph{Theorem 3 (Reduced Fourier nonvanishing criterion).}
After microscopic tensor reduction to the shell-transverse standard form, the shell-level transverse
Dirac coefficients are nonzero exactly when
\[
\boxed{
(C^\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
Immediate from the Fourier formula above. \(\square\)

\subsection{What is automatic and what is not}

We now separate the parts that are automatic from the parts that remain open.

\paragraph{Automatic once a gradient-linear enriched tensor exists:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item reduction to shell-transverse form
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha;
\]

\item first-shell Fourier support of \(\mathcal T^\alpha\);

\item the shell-level projected transverse matrices have the correct traceless internal Pauli form.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Still not automatic:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item nonvanishing of
\[
C^\alpha\cdot G_*;
\]

\item survival of two independent internal directions after projection;

\item spectral isolation of the enriched shell block.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the remaining microscopic work has been narrowed to a finite tensor-coefficient problem.

\subsection{Sharp final theorem of this step}

\paragraph{Theorem 4 (Sharp microscopic reduction theorem).}
Suppose the microscopic TECT linearization contains a nonzero gradient-linear enriched tensor
coupling on an internal doublet,
\[
\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
\mathsf N_{ij}^{a}\,
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,
(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a,
\]
and that after shell-transverse projection two internal traceless directions survive:
\[
a=1,2.
\]
Then the shell-level Dirac problem is reduced to verifying only:
\[
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
C^1\cdot G_*\neq0,
\qquad
C^2\cdot G_*\neq0,
\]
together with the previously established conditions
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq0,
\]
and spectral isolation of the enriched shell block.

\paragraph{Proof.}
Theorem 1 gives the shell-transverse form. Theorem 3 gives the exact nonvanishing criterion.
The earlier shell-Dirac theorem then completes the argument. \(\square\)

\section{Final Summary}

A general gradient-linear enriched coupling in the microscopic TECT linearization has the form
\[
\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
\mathsf N_{ij}^{a}\,
(\partial_i\phi_0(x))\,
(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\]

After choosing a shell direction \(G_*\) and projecting to the transverse shell plane, this always
reduces to
\[
\mathcal T^{\alpha a}(x)=C^{\alpha a}{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x),
\qquad
C^{\alpha a}{}_j=e^\alpha_i\,\mathsf N_{ij}^{a}.
\]

Therefore the previously used shell-level ansatz
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha
\]
is exactly the canonical shell-transverse reduction of the most general gradient-linear enriched
microscopic tensor coupling.

The corresponding shell Fourier coefficient is
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)
=
i(C^\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\,s^\alpha.
\]

Hence, once a nonzero gradient-linear enriched tensor exists and two internal Pauli directions
survive projection, the only remaining microscopic nonvanishing conditions are
\[
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
C^1\cdot G_*\neq0,
\qquad
C^2\cdot G_*\neq0,
\]
together with the already established
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq0,
\]
and spectral isolation of the enriched shell block.

Thus the remaining shell-level Dirac task has been reduced to a finite microscopic tensor-coefficient
problem plus spectral isolation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Dirac Emergence: Microscopic Reduction to Tensor Coefficients}

\subsection{Logical status}

At the present stage, the emergence of the Dirac operator in the TECT framework
should be formulated neither as a purely geometric slogan
\[
\mathbb{CP}^2 \Longrightarrow \text{Dirac}
\]
nor as an already completed microscopic theorem of the full BCC Bloch problem.

What has been established is a layered structure:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a rigorous minimal reduced Dirac theorem at the level of a projected
infrared sector;

\item an explicit improved effective realization in a \( \mathbb{CP}^2 \)-projector
defect model, including a full-rank mixed symbol at the effective level;

\item a microscopic shell-level reduction showing that the remaining open problem
is no longer conceptual, but reduces to a finite tensor-coefficient and spectral
isolation problem.
\end{enumerate}

This section summarizes that chain in its strongest honest form.

\subsection{Minimal reduced Dirac theorem}

Let \(\mathcal L(p)\) denote the relevant linearized operator near the low-energy
point \(p=0\). Suppose:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(R1)] there exists an isolated complex \(4\)-dimensional infrared sector
\[
\mathcal K,\qquad \dim_{\mathbb C}\mathcal K=4;
\]

\item[(R2)] \(\mathcal K\) carries an involution
\[
J^\dagger=J,\qquad J^2=\mathbf 1,
\]
with splitting
\[
\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus \mathcal K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}\mathcal K_\pm=2;
\]

\item[(R3)] after subtraction of the common reference energy, the leading projected
operator is odd under \(J\):
\[
\mathcal D_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
=
\Pi_{\mathcal K}\mathcal L(p)\Pi_{\mathcal K}
=
\mathcal D_1(p)+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
J\mathcal D_1J^{-1}=-\mathcal D_1;
\]

\item[(R4)] in a basis adapted to \(\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus\mathcal K_-\),
\[
\mathcal D_1(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\]
and the mixed symbol \(A_1(p)\) is nondegenerate for generic small \(p\neq0\).
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Theorem 1 (Minimal reduced Dirac emergence).}
Under \((R1)\)--\((R4)\), the principal infrared operator is unitarily equivalent,
after a linear momentum redefinition, to the massless Dirac operator:
\[
\mathcal D_1(p)\sim p_i\alpha^i,
\qquad
\{\alpha^i,\alpha^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
Oddness under \(J\) forces the diagonal \(++\) and \(--\) blocks of \(\mathcal D_1\)
to vanish. Thus the operator is block-off-diagonal.
A nondegenerate \(2\times2\) complex first-order Hermitian symbol is reducible,
after basis changes and linear momentum redefinition, to Pauli form
\[
A_1(p)\sim p_i\sigma^i.
\]
The full \(4\times4\) operator is therefore
\[
\mathcal D_1(p)\sim
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & p_i\sigma^i\\
p_i\sigma^i & 0
\end{pmatrix}
=
p_i\alpha^i,
\]
which is the massless Dirac principal operator. \(\square\)

\subsection{Effective realization in the \( \mathbb{CP}^2 \)-projector defect sector}

In the effective \( \mathbb{CP}^2 \)-projector description, let
\[
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger
\]
be a reflection-symmetric static defect background. Tangent fluctuations may be
written as
\[
\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger + z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger\eta=0,
\]
so the fluctuation field takes values in
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}Q_B=2.
\]

For the explicit local representative
\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\]
an orthonormal frame is
\[
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
In this frame the transverse \(Q_B\)-connection vanishes:
\[
\mathcal A_\xi=-i\,e^\dagger\partial_\xi e=0.
\]

The local static Hessian therefore reduces to a channel Schr\"odinger operator
\[
\mathcal H_B^{\mathrm{stat}}
=
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2+\mathcal U_B(\xi).
\]

With the improved two-anisotropy effective potential
\[
V(P)=
-\frac{\lambda}{2}\mathrm{Tr}([H,P]^2)
-\frac{\mu}{2}\mathrm{Tr}([K,P]^2),
\]
where
\[
H=\mathrm{diag}(1,0,-1),
\qquad
K=\mathrm{diag}(1,-1,-1),
\qquad
\lambda,\mu>0,
\]
the static channels become
\[
H_1
=
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2
+
(\lambda+\mu)\cos^2 2\theta(\xi)-2\rho\,\theta'(\xi)^2,
\]
\[
H_2
=
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2
+
\lambda+2\mu\cos^2\theta(\xi)-\rho\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]

For explicit even defect profiles such as
\[
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\operatorname{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\]
variational estimates show that both channels can support low even/odd bound
states in a nonempty parameter regime at the effective-model level.

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
This gives strong effective support for an isolated \(4\)-mode infrared sector,
though not yet a full microscopic proof.

\subsection{Why the plain scalar BCC Bloch pair is not enough}

Consider instead a minimal periodic scalar Bloch problem around the BCC background
\[
\phi_0(x)=2A\sum_{a=1}^{6}\cos(Q_a\cdot x).
\]
The corresponding Bloch Hessian has the reciprocal-harmonic form
\[
\bigl(H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\bigr)_{G,G'}
=
h_0(k+G)\delta_{GG'}+U_{G-G'}.
\]
The minimal two-harmonic Bragg truncation near the correct Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}
\]
yields
\[
H_{\mathrm{pair}}(p)
=
E_0(p)\mathbf 1
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau^3
+
m\,\tau^1
+
O(|p|^2).
\]

\paragraph{Proposition 2.}
The minimal scalar Bragg pair does not generically produce a Weyl cone by itself.

\paragraph{Reason.}
Its linear traceless symbol is only one-dimensional at principal order, so it
does not supply the full \(3\)-direction Pauli structure required for Weyl/Dirac.

Thus a genuine shell-level Dirac theorem requires an enriched shell space.

\subsection{Minimal enriched shell space}

The minimal enriched shell carrier is
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
where the shell pair provides one Pauli sector and the internal doublet provides
the missing two transverse traceless generators.

Let \(\tau^a\) act on the pair sector and \(s^a\) on the internal sector. Then
\[
\Gamma^1=\tau^1\otimes s^1,
\qquad
\Gamma^2=\tau^1\otimes s^2,
\qquad
\Gamma^3=\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1
\]
satisfy
\[
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\]

Therefore
\[
H_{\mathrm{Dirac}}(p)
=
v_1p_1\,\tau^1\otimes s^1
+
v_2p_2\,\tau^1\otimes s^2
+
v_3p_3\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1
\]
is an exact massless Dirac principal operator on the enriched shell space.

\paragraph{Conclusion.}
The plain scalar Bloch pair is insufficient, but the internal doublet
\(\otimes\) shell pair is sufficient in principle for shell-level Dirac emergence.

\subsection{Shell-level projected matrix-element theorem}

Choose shell basis states
\[
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad a=1,2,
\]
where \(u_a(x)\) span the internal periodic shell envelopes.

Projecting the Bloch Hamiltonian to the enriched shell sector gives
\[
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The shell-level Dirac theorem requires:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(S1)] \(B_0:=B(0)=0\);
\item[(S2)] \(E_+(p)-E_-(p)=2v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\mathbf 1_2+O(|p|^2)\) with
\(v_\parallel\neq0\);
\item[(S3)] \(B(p)=p_1W^1+p_2W^2+O(|p|^2)\), where \(W^1,W^2\) are traceless Hermitian,
nonzero, and anticommuting after internal basis reduction.
\end{enumerate}

Under these conditions,
\[
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
\sim
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1
+
\nu_1 p_1\,\tau^1\otimes s^1
+
\nu_2 p_2\,\tau^1\otimes s^2,
\]
hence the projected shell Hamiltonian is Dirac.

\subsection{Constant-envelope reduction and Fourier selection rules}

For the simplest constant-envelope ansatz
\[
u_a(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}\xi_a,
\qquad
\xi_a^\dagger\xi_b=\delta_{ab},
\]
the shell-level quantities reduce to primitive-cell Fourier coefficients:
\[
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2,
\]
\[
W^\alpha=\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)\,s^\alpha.
\]

If the scalar periodic potential is generated quadratically from the first-shell
BCC condensate, for example
\[
U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)\propto \phi_0(x)^2,
\]
then a quadratic first-shell selection rule gives
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\]
hence
\[
B_0=0.
\]

Thus the dangerous constant Bragg mass vanishes automatically in the simplest
first-shell quadratic scalar setting.

\subsection{Classification of enriched couplings}

We classify enriched coefficient fields \(\mathcal T^\alpha(x)\) into low-order types:

\begin{enumerate}
\item linear in \(\phi_0\),
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha\sim \phi_0;
\]

\item linear in derivatives,
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha\sim \partial_j\phi_0;
\]

\item quadratic,
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha\sim \phi_0^2,\quad \phi_0\partial\phi_0,\quad
(\partial\phi_0)^2.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Only the linear classes generically retain first-shell Fourier support.
Purely quadratic enriched couplings generally shift support to sums of shell
vectors and are therefore not minimal shell-Dirac candidates.

The most natural minimal allowed class is therefore
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
\]

\subsection{Microscopic tensor reduction theorem}

Now let the microscopic TECT linearization contain a general gradient-linear
enriched term
\[
\delta\mathcal L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
\mathsf N_{ij}^{a}\,
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,
(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\]

Choose the shell direction
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}
\]
and a transverse basis \(e^\alpha_i\), \(\alpha=1,2\), satisfying
\[
e^\alpha_i\hat n_i=0.
\]
Projecting the first spatial index onto the shell-transverse plane gives
\[
C^{\alpha a}{}_j=e^\alpha_i\,\mathsf N_{ij}^{a}.
\]
Hence the shell-transverse enriched coefficient fields are
\[
\mathcal T^{\alpha a}(x)=C^{\alpha a}{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x).
\]

\paragraph{Theorem 3 (Microscopic tensor reduction).}
Any gradient-linear enriched microscopic tensor coupling on an internal doublet
reduces, after shell-transverse projection, to the standard shell form
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha
\]
for the surviving two internal Pauli directions.

Thus the shell-level ansatz is not ad hoc: it is the canonical shell-transverse
reduction of the most general gradient-linear microscopic enriched tensor.

\subsection{Final microscopic nonvanishing criterion}

Using the first-shell Fourier expansion
\[
\phi_0(x)=\sum_{G\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}A_G e^{iG\cdot x},
\]
we obtain
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)
=
i(C^\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\,s^\alpha.
\]

Therefore the final shell-transverse nonvanishing condition is
\[
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
C^1\cdot G_*\neq0,
\qquad
C^2\cdot G_*\neq0.
\]

Combining everything, the shell-level Dirac problem is reduced to the following
finite conditions:

\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
C^1\cdot G_*\neq0,
\qquad
C^2\cdot G_*\neq0,
\]
plus spectral isolation of the enriched shell block.

\subsection{What is proved and what remains open}

What is proved:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal reduced Dirac theorem;

\item explicit effective realizability in the improved \( \mathbb{CP}^2 \)-defect model;

\item the plain scalar shell-pair obstruction;

\item the necessity of the enriched shell space
\[
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}};
\]

\item shell-level reduction to projected matrix elements;

\item vanishing of the constant Bragg mass by a quadratic first-shell selection
rule;

\item classification of allowed enriched couplings;

\item reduction of the microscopic shell problem to finite tensor coefficients.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open:

\begin{enumerate}
\item explicit identification of a nonzero microscopic gradient-linear enriched
tensor \(\mathsf N_{ij}^{a}\) in the actual TECT linearization;

\item verification that two shell-transverse projections survive with
\[
C^1\cdot G_*\neq0,
\qquad
C^2\cdot G_*\neq0;
\]

\item spectral isolation of the enriched shell block in the actual Bloch spectrum.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the remaining gap is no longer conceptual. It is a finite microscopic
tensor-coefficient problem plus a spectral-isolation problem.

\section{Final Summary}

The emergence of the Dirac operator in the present TECT framework is now reduced
to a sharply defined microscopic problem.

At the abstract level, the following is rigorously proved:

if there exists an isolated graded complex four-dimensional infrared sector with
nondegenerate mixed first-order symbol, then the principal operator is Dirac.

At the effective level, this structure is explicitly realizable in an improved
\(\mathbb{CP}^2\)-projector defect model.

At the shell-Bloch level, the plain scalar Bragg pair is not sufficient by
itself, but the enriched shell space
\[
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
is sufficient in principle.

The shell-level problem has been reduced to the standard coupling form
\[
\mathcal T^\alpha(x)=C^\alpha{}_j\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s^\alpha,
\qquad \alpha=1,2,
\]
which arises canonically from the shell-transverse reduction of the most general
gradient-linear enriched microscopic tensor coupling
\[
\mathsf N_{ij}^{a}\,
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,
(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\]

The final microscopic conditions are therefore:

\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
C^1\cdot G_*\neq0,
\qquad
C^2\cdot G_*\neq0,
\]
together with spectral isolation of the enriched shell block.

Hence the remaining shell-level Dirac problem is reduced to a finite
tensor-coefficient problem plus a spectral-isolation problem.
